    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546150229?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller?shelf=my-library-catalogue">my-library-catalogue</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546150229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9088587429815233212">Via <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.nikihawkes.com'>www.nikihawkes.com</a><br/><br/>[4.5 stars] Anything Richelle Mead writes is golden, and this book is another example of why she is one of my favorite authors! From the prologue all the way to the last page, I was completely entertained by the story, the world, and the character development. Set as a futuristic urban fantasy, which is original in itself, the novel draws from worldwide mythology, making it one of the most unique books I’ve read in a while. Top that off with crime-solving detective work and</span>
  <span id="freeText9088587429815233212" style="display:none">Via <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nikihawkes.com">www.nikihawkes.com</a><br /><br />[4.5 stars] Anything Richelle Mead writes is golden, and this book is another example of why she is one of my favorite authors! From the prologue all the way to the last page, I was completely entertained by the story, the world, and the character development. Set as a futuristic urban fantasy, which is original in itself, the novel draws from worldwide mythology, making it one of the most unique books I’ve read in a while. Top that off with crime-solving detective work and just a touch of romance, and you have yourself a killer novel! I always appreciate Mead for her originality and creativity, and I think she might have outdone herself here.<br /><br />A few weeks ago I criticized an author for switching perspectives and having too many things going on at once for me to feel invested in the story and the characters. Gameboard of the Gods is a shining example of how to weave multiple storylines without losing any momentum. Each perspective was intertwined with the main plot and they were introduced in a way that allowed me time to develop a sense for each person and their inner demons. Every protagonist directly added to the building of the plot, which is the best way to keep readers from becoming distracted when the perspective switches. <br /><br />I thought the character development was one of the strongest elements of the story. I always marvel about how she can make flawed characters so likable. Maybe it’s because they come across as real human beings, rather than ideal figments of the author’s mind. Right from the beginning, we know a bit about what drives these characters and the inner conflicts they face. The prologue where we meet Mae was incredibly powerful; my only wish is that Mead would’ve represented the physical representations of her flaws a bit more throughout the book. In any case, I won’t be forgetting these characters any time soon.<br /><br />Overall, the storyline was fantastic – plenty of intelligent plot decisions, the perfect amount of complexity, and a snowballing momentum that will keep you up all night. It was truly a well-conceived book, and I am doubly excited to see where she takes it next!<br /><br />Other books you might like:<br /><br />Succubus Blues by Richelle Mead (my favorite of her works)<br />Divergent by Veronica Roth<br />Survival by Julie E. Czerneda<br />Moon Called by Patricia Briggs<br />Grimspace by Ann Aguirre<br />Dead Witch Walking by Kim Harrison</span>
  <a data-text-id="9088587429815233212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer598625514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10207543144494126828"><b>VLOG REVIEW:</b><br/><br/><b>I've made a VLOG REVIEW of GAMEBOARD OF THE GODS. <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rH_83PMpU3A' rel='nofollow noopener'>CLICK HERE TO WATCH IT.</a></b><br/><br/>P.S. DO NOT LAUGH. My accent is weird, I know. Sarreh.<br/><br/><b>WRITTEN REVIEW:</b><br/><br/>I'll be completely honest here. I totally didn't know what to expect from Gameboard of the Gods, which is kinda bizarre considering Richelle Mead is kind of already a household name with her <i>Vampire Academy</i> and <i>Bloodlines</i> series. I bought her first book sometime ago and read the first 10 pages and was truthfully not impressed; the writing felt </span>
  <span id="freeText10207543144494126828" style="display:none"><b>VLOG REVIEW:</b><br><br><b>I've made a VLOG REVIEW of GAMEBOARD OF THE GODS. <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rH_83PMpU3A" rel="nofollow noopener">CLICK HERE TO WATCH IT.</a></b><br><br>P.S. DO NOT LAUGH. My accent is weird, I know. Sarreh.<br><br><b>WRITTEN REVIEW:</b><br><br>I'll be completely honest here. I totally didn't know what to expect from Gameboard of the Gods, which is kinda bizarre considering Richelle Mead is kind of already a household name with her <i>Vampire Academy</i> and <i>Bloodlines</i> series. I bought her first book sometime ago and read the first 10 pages and was truthfully not impressed; the writing felt a bit amateur, bland, and empty, making me a bit less eager to read something from her this time around. But <i>Vampire Academy</i> was written so many years ago, and considering the fact that it has been ages since then, her writing must have become better.<br><br>And it did. Significantly so. If <i>Vampire Academy </i> didn't reach out to me in the first ten pages, <i>Gameboard of the Gods</i> did, and every time I think of this gem of a book, all I can think of is just how awesome and suspenseful it was. <b>If you thought her previous series were good, THIS is <u>BETTER.</u></b><br><br><b>
  <u>WORLD BUILDING - AMAZING!</u>
</b><br><br>The world building here is at its finest. It's big, it's ambitious, it's incredibly structured and imaginative, and it's not even fantasy at all - far from it! Imagine a Greek-Roman society but make it a bit futuristic, as well as ancient mythological gods and goddesses from different cultures. I loved how it incorporated such religious deities and themes while also staying true to its futuristic utopian setting (yes, it's <u>not</u> a dystopian!). I also loved how Mead portrayed a supposedly pagan community that thrives on idealistic and radical ideas, while also introducing to us a variety of gods, goddesses, and supernatural phenomena. Like, how can the two mix, right?! That's basically a juxtaposition right there, but she does it right and does it well. I'm not going to venture too much about it, because saying so might give something away about the storyline, but I can instead assure you that the author has created an absolutely thrilling and engaging world you won't get enough of. Add gods and goddesses to that mix, fanatic cults, superhuman folks, AND a radical government, you got yourself a unique and exciting formula there, my friend!<br><br><b>
  <u>CHARACTERS - WELL-ROUNDED, WHILE AT TIMES INFURIATING</u>
</b><br><br>Don't get me wrong, I <i>loved</i> the characters. The cast all had distinguishable personalities, had distinct voices, were smart, feisty, and level-headed, knew what they wanted and how to get it, and over-all were pretty well-rounded. But even though they were likeable most of the times, they did some actions that really infuriated me, as in, I actually would throw them out the window if I could. These times were mostly when they acted like an asshole and a bitch, though... like, there was this one instance that some characters withheld information that could've helped the case, and the excuse, "I forgot", and "I didn't think it was important!" made me want to go HULK, SMASH!! on them. <br><br>But then again, after giving it much thought, it made me realize that these reactions of mine were only because of Mead's spectacular way of making me more involved and engaged with the character, to the point that I would feel for them. They do something great, I feel happy. They do something questionable, I feel angry because as a reader I have more understanding with regards to the context/situation, and I freaking know what they did wasn't healthy. You have to applaud Mead for that... it's not often I get angry at characters and find such a response being a good thing!<br><br><b>
  <u>WRITING - SPECTACULAR!</u>
</b><br><br>As I've gushed earlier, Mead has significantly improved her writing style here. Yes, I know; I only have 10 pages of Vampire Academy for comparison, but damn, the difference was just astounding! Given that the plot is darker and sinister, she was able to write it in a way that's consistent to the premise - the narration really does give you the impression that something malicious and evil is or will be happening, while also keeping you on your toes and at the edges of your seats. It is suspenseful and enchanting, and the prose is hard to resist, as Mead has showcased here her remarkable skill of "showing, not telling" style. Even though the narration is set in third person with multiple POVs, it was still able to successfully give me a clear view of the surroundings, while also allowing me into the thoughts of the characters. You will get to know them and love every minute of it.<br><br>The relationships among the characters were also brilliantly written. Even though something ridiculous happened in the beginning that I really couldn't appreciate, it redeems itself when the characters start from square one, finding themselves entangled <s>unwillingly</s> in a mystery whodunit story. Along the way they will banter with each other, argue with each other, discuss theories and logistics together, and protect one another and you will find all of these in the end absolutely endearing. It was definitely a meaningful journey to me seeing them grow, learn more about themselves, and find each other's worth.<br><br><b>OVERALL...</b><br><br>Altogether, this is a remarkable sci-fi, PR, mystery read. It's an Adult book that would rile up your imagination and excite your nerves as you charge head-on to a fascinating world Mead has created. Since there're a lot of themes that I personally deem sensitive to certain audiences (sex, drugs, alcohol, the works), I don't recommend this for those 15 below, but if you're mentally and emotionally mature for it, then go ahead! <br><br>All I can say is <i>Gameboard of the Gods</i> is Richelle Mead's best yet.<br><br><b>Final verdict: 4.5 stars</b><br><br>Read this and my other reviews + giveaways at The Social Potato.<br><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="The Social Potato Reviews" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380266349i/682124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440948886?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440948886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7580577085869178827"><b>Gameboard of the Gods</b> is something entirely different from author Richelle Mead. No vampires, no succubi, no fae. Instead, the reader is treated to a fast-paced mystery thriller with some supernatural elements. <br/><br/>The world is intriguing: a sort of post-apocalyptic world devastated by a virus that wiped out half the population. The remaining survivors suffer from all sorts of genetic woes: poor fertility, asthma, damaged hair and skin. In this world, organized religion is banned. Only state approve</span>
  <span id="freeText7580577085869178827" style="display:none"><b>Gameboard of the Gods</b> is something entirely different from author Richelle Mead. No vampires, no succubi, no fae. Instead, the reader is treated to a fast-paced mystery thriller with some supernatural elements. <br /><br />The world is intriguing: a sort of post-apocalyptic world devastated by a virus that wiped out half the population. The remaining survivors suffer from all sorts of genetic woes: poor fertility, asthma, damaged hair and skin. In this world, organized religion is banned. Only state approved religion and churches are allowed to exist. The state is the higher authority. <br /><br />On a more sinister side, genetic manipulations have been made in order to counteract the effects of the virus. Each citizen is given a genetic rating based upon their genetic background. The higher the number, the more likely that person could reproduce a genetically healthy offspring. <br /><br />The story focuses upon two characters. Mae is a Praetorian, an elite soldier with a special implant that gives her speed and strength. Mae does have a dark side to her, and it is quite scary. Justin is a Servitor who has lived in exile in the south. Justin has a few demons of his own, and he hears the voices of two ravens in his head. (loved them!) Mae and Justin are assigned to solve a serial murder that appears to be ritualistic and occurs every full moon. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this story, probably because Vancouver was the capital of the Republic of North America. It’s so much fun to see my hometown in books! I found the world absolutely fascinating, especially how the state tried to thwart religion and replace it with its own authority. I loved how the author incorporated folklore about the gods into the narrative. <br /><br /><b>Gameboard of the Gods</b> is a solid start to an original series. Fans of Richelle Mead’s adult books would enjoy this book. My only criticism and it is minor – I was left wanting more! I can’t wait for the next book which does not yet have a publication date. <br /><br />Check out the author’s webpage for more information on <b>Gameboard of the Gods</b>. She has a glossary of terms, and all sorts of background information <a>here</a>.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Edelweiss and Dutton for a review copy of this book. </i><br /><br /><b>Review posted on <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews</a></b>.<br /></span>

<div id="review_635545613" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635545613" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/635545613?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101624302" href="/book/show/17664518-gameboard-of-the-gods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=religious-elements">religious-elements</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=wtfery">wtfery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=slow-paced">slow-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=rubbish-worldbuilding">rubbish-worldbuilding</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring-crap-hero">boring-crap-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=powers">powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah-romance">blah-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=hero-boring">hero-boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635545613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14324378340603388417"><b>2.5 stars - Spoilers</b><br/><br/>I was tempted to give this 3 stars but I decided not to since the worldbuilding (especially in the first half) was such a mess. It did improve somewhat in the latter half but it was a case of too little, too late. I do still want to read the sequel because there was potential, and I have to say that by the end I did find myself invested in the story and characters (well, some of the characters). <br/><br/>-The worldbuilding was a <i>massive</i> let down. I had no idea what the hell was going </span>
  <span id="freeText14324378340603388417" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars - Spoilers</b><br /><br />I was tempted to give this 3 stars but I decided not to since the worldbuilding (especially in the first half) was such a mess. It did improve somewhat in the latter half but it was a case of too little, too late. I do still want to read the sequel because there was potential, and I have to say that by the end I did find myself invested in the story and characters (well, some of the characters). <br /><br />-The worldbuilding was a <i>massive</i> let down. I had no idea what the hell was going on. Most of the terminology used came with no explanation whatsoever… It wasn't just that there was no explanation, there was also very little context given. How was I meant to figure out what things like castal, praetoria, plebian, Nordic, Gemman and RUNA meant? Yes, most was explained later on, but for the first half I was utterly lost. It wasn't until 20% in that I finally knew what the hell RUNA stood for. <br />It took me a while to figure out the whole praetorian malarkey — they were RUNA super soldiers that for some reason were divided in to different colours. I'm still not sure if the colours were indicative of rank, skill, experience or if it was just random… I don't think it was ever mentioned.<br />I also didn't know what the castes/plebians were until a third of the way through. And even then I was further confused by each person having a score of some kind. <br />The worldbuilding for the majority of the book was vague and nonsensical. It was frustrating to read, and it severely lessened my enjoyment.<br /><br />-The vague history/background/thinking on religion, race, the Republic etc.. annoyed me. I didn't know why things were the way they were — there were few clues/hints given as to why the world was the way it was. I was actually hoping for an info-dump.<br /><br />-I liked Mae's character. Her cool, composed and strong personality was a nice change from the usual heroine. She was the character that was most engaging for me.<br /><br />-I hated Justin's character. He was the typical self-pitying, loser, manslut. Why did everyone keep saying he was charming? He wasn't. Why did everyone (including himself) say he was brilliant and genius like? I didn't see any evidence of that. Most of the time he just stated the obvious, and occasionally he'd come to logical conclusions that anyone with half a brain could come to.<br />The only thing that was somewhat interesting about him were his ravens. However, I was irritated that the origin/story behind the ravens wasn't explained until 60% in. They were a big part of Justin's character but there was no explanation for them for over half the story. I was baffled as to whether they were real or in his mind, and if they were helping Justin or if they had their own agenda. I don't know why they were left unexplained for so long.<br />The worst thing about Justin was the whole Tessa thing. Why the fuck did Justin take 16yr old Tessa to RUNA with him only to then dump her on his sister to look after? He didn't even ask his sister's permission. And Tessa is his responsibility but he just palmed her off. If a family member dumped some random kid on me, I'd tell them to piss off and look after said kid themselves. Especially if that family member was off having fun and getting laid. How dare Justin take a child from their family and promise to look after them only to just palm them off on a stranger?! Justin was vile.<br /><br />-I wasn't impressed with Justin and Mae's relationship, it was so shallow. Justin only liked Mae because of her drop dead gorgeous looks, and Mae only seemed to want Justin because he was sexy and good in bed. Their instant connection was ridiculous. It was made even more ridiculous because Justin was still horny for loads of other girls and was fucking any girl he met. It was dumb that he slutted around but then got all poetic about Mae. Am I meant to believe he's in love with her something? I don't. It'd help if he wasn't screwing dozens of other girls because he's just that horny. <br />It also didn't help that Justin came across as really wimpy and weak when compared to Mae. He didn't need to be some badass fighter but he could have at least tried to protect himself instead of sitting back and watching Mae get beaten and put in danger for him. I hate guys like that. <br /> <br />-If Justin believed in the supernatural and the existence of gods and had seen evidence of both… Why was he so adamant that the shadow that killed a bunch of people wasn't supernatural and was in fact some sort of human trick?<br /><br />-Tessa. What was the point of her? Why was she a main/POV character when she added little to the actual story? She seemed to be a tool to 1. Make Justin seem a bit more relatable and 2. To observe the RUNA and its way of life. She was pointless to the main story arc… A main character needs be involved more than that. Maybe in book 2 she'll actually serve a purpose to the story.<br /><br />-The murder mystery was quite interesting. It did get a bit silly with all the cheesy religious cults and brainwashed cult members murdering for a higher power. I think it would have worked better if it wasn't written so cartoony with underground lairs, evul masks, dark robes and other such nonsense. <br /><br />-WTF's an ego? A phone? A tablet? Anytime an ego would be mentioned I kept thinking of a person's ego rather than the device/technology the characters were using. Why couldn't RM have given the "ego" a name that wouldn't remind readers of something else?<br /><br />-Why was Geraki suddenly called Demetrius Devereaux?<br /><br />-So was Dominic an AWOL praetorian??<br /><br />All in all, it was disappointing. I wasn't impressed with the worldbuilding or Justin's character… But I'm willing to give the second book a go since 1. It has potential and 2. Mae was my kind of heroine (well, except when she wasn't being all pathetic and desperate for disgusting Justin).</span>
  <a data-text-id="14324378340603388417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8587873405887785971"><b>'<i>I am a soldier of the Republic. I do not serve my own will but that of my country.</i> Those words were echoed by her mother's, spoken so many years ago: <i>You can ignore the rest because you're better than them. Empty yourself of all feeling because if they can't see it, then they can't use it against you.</i>'</b><br/><br/>Richelle Mead's story-weaving genius comes to life in her new series <i>Age of X</i>.   <span id="freeText8587873405887785971" style="display:none"><b>'<i>I am a soldier of the Republic. I do not serve my own will but that of my country.</i> Those words were echoed by her mother's, spoken so many years ago: <i>You can ignore the rest because you're better than them. Empty yourself of all feeling because if they can't see it, then they can't use it against you.</i>'</b><br /><br />Richelle Mead's story-weaving genius comes to life in her new series <i>Age of X</i>. Be prepared to fall head first into her futuristic world, filled with mystery, violence, stunning technology and tension bubbling just below the surface - be prepared to fall in love with a story, and a cast of characters, you will never forget. <br /><br /><b>'"We're all pieces on a game board, Dr. March, and some of us are more powerful than others. You. Me. Her. We're the ones the gods want. We're the ones they're fighting over."<br />"And I supposed you consider yourself the king on this board?"<br />"You must not have played chess in a while. The king is the weakest piece in the game." He gave Justin a level look. "The queen's the strongest."'</b><br /><br />Meet <b>Justin March</b>: exile, genius, former investigator of religious groups and supernatural claims, notorious wine drinker, and charmer of the female demographic. <br /><br />Meet <b>Mae Koskinen</b>: Nordic, beautiful, deadly and dedicated praetorian - a member of the military’s most elite and intimidating tier...a soldier with enhanced reflexes and skills.<br /><br /><b>Neither, upon meeting the other, ever suspected how tightly bound their fates would become.</b><br /><br />Mae, currently relieved of her duties, is sent to bring Justin back to RUNA - the Republic of United North America. But the chance to go back isn't as golden as it seems. There's a catch. Justin is assigned a difficult and dangerous task, to solve a string of ritualistic murders. To keep Justin safe, he is assigned a guard...who turns out to be none other than Mae. The girl who Justin has been told about - the girl involved in a strange prophecy of sorts. <br /><br />A girl coveted by the gods. A girl he can never have.<br /><br /><b>'"The old guy said I'd only need one woman, and that the one he'd send me would mirror me in light and shadow, that I'd know her by a crown of flowers...He said she'd be carved of fire and ice, that she'd scorch me in my bed and live and die for me outside of it."</b><br /><br />But solving the murders is no easy task. The clues are an incoherent jumble, no connections visible in the tangle of deaths, religious oddities and supernatural occurrences. Every lead seems to stop at an abrupt dead end. The deeper the duo delve into the mystery, the more exposed to danger they become. <br /><br /><b>And they only have four weeks to find the murderer and solve the case.</b><br /><br />Mundane murderers and cults aren't Mae and Justin's only problems, though. Other forces are at work...old forces. Powerful forces. Ones that will do anything and everything to claim what is rightfully theirs, be that the world, or those upon it. Playing with fire may be dangerous, but playing on the chessboard of the gods is a <i>whole</i> other game...one that could cost them their lives.<br /><br /><b>What will the 'Age of X' entail for humankind? And are the gods closer than you think?<b><br /><br />Mythology, romance and kick-ass adventure combine to create a vivid dystopian world that will sweep you away and have you hooked from the first page to the very last word.</b></b></span>

<div id="review_499832369" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/499832369" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/499832369?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomoe Hotaru" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru">Tomoe Hotaru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=not-my-cuppa-tea">not-my-cuppa-tea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer499832369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3063685528607168674"><b>
  <u>16 Jun '13</u>
</b><br/>Please be warned that this review contains spoilers and language some people may find distasteful.<br/><br/><b>Post-reading:</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404185i/786472.jpg' width='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When I heard this would be an <i>adult</i> novel, I was expecting something that read more maturely. Sex scenes and drug use does not an adult novel make. In fact, <i>controversial themes</i> does not an adult novel make.<br/>While I was looking forward to something deep -- a decidedly more <i>mature</i> tone in narrative, and a plot that does not reek so much of post-pubescent sexual drama -- what</span>
  <span id="freeText3063685528607168674" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>16 Jun '13</u>
</b><br>Please be warned that this review contains spoilers and language some people may find distasteful.<br><br><b>Post-reading:</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404185i/786472.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I heard this would be an <i>adult</i> novel, I was expecting something that read more maturely. Sex scenes and drug use does not an adult novel make. In fact, <i>controversial themes</i> does not an adult novel make.<br>While I was looking forward to something deep -- a decidedly more <i>mature</i> tone in narrative, and a plot that does not reek so much of post-pubescent sexual drama -- what I received instead was just another strung up excuse to merge the rapidly overused tropes of forbidden love, handsome men and beautiful women, and alluringly assholeish love interests, under the pretense of a futuristic murder-mystery amidst a divine war.<br><br>That's right. <b><i>Gameboard of the Gods</i> would just be another one of your average YA Paranormal Romance series,</b> weren't it for our main characters' older age-range and some sex scenes and drug abuse thrown in there.<br><br>For a start, all that talk about <i>"working together to solve a string of ritualistic murders"</i> the blurb so cunningly deceived me into looking forward to, did not actually make an active appearance in this novel until well past the 50% mark. And trust me when I say this was one <i>long</i> book, making <b>the first half an extended experience of pure boredom</b>.<br>Of course, if you enjoy reading about sexual tension and attempts of character build-up for over 200 pages, you may have a better experience than I did.<br>Now, I am usually a patient reader; I strive for character drama, I love vividly drawn and fleshed out personalities -- but only if it is done well. <i>Gameboard of the Gods</i> indeed attempted to do all that. Unfortunately, what was <i>meant</i> to be flashbacks and recounts for the purpose of justifying our main characters' current personalities, instead became thinly veiled disguises to further demonstrate their sexual prowess and lovelife.<br><br>I didn't care about how Mae and Porfirio <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(seriously, what is UP with that name?!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> met for the first time, or how they <i>fucked</i> for the first time. But I had to read about it <i>twice</i> in two separate chapters. It did not progress the story in any way, nor did it provide any believable insight into Mae's character. So the girl likes to fuck, and is good at it. I could already tell by the way Justin kept going on and on about seeing that infamous <i>"crown of stars and flowers"</i> on her orgasm-face. I <i>certainly</i> did not need to read about Porfirio and Mae.<br>Her relationship with her family was perhaps more interesting in terms of drama. It gave more understanding to the way Mae was raised and how it shaped her as a character. However these <b>subsidiary characters were flat, unidimensional, and just plain laughable</b>.<br>This half-effort can be forgiven though, seeing as this is the first in a series, and the book was already far too long for my liking without throwing in fully-fleshed background characters.<br><br>Moving on from Mae, let us take a look at Justin. Our flirtatious, bastardly good-looking hero. Aside from being an <b>obvious male-love-interest stereotype</b>, there was one other thing I just couldn't help notice.<br><br>Justin March is gay.<br><br>And I do <b>not</b> mean that as an insult or belittlement in any way. It is simply an observation.<br><br>How else do you explain a man who knows <i>way</i> too much about clothes? Down to the fact of <i>the year it came out</i>??<br>Oh, there was a half-arsed attempt to explain his expertise in ladies' fashion:<br><blockquote>The woman's dress was a deep plum crepe de chine, with no sleeves and a high neckline.<br><br><i>Who in the world knows what crepe de chine is?</i> asked Horatio.<br><br><i>I had to learn that stuff a long time ago,</i> Justin said.</blockquote><br><br>Well I laugh at your poor attempt to explain away something completely irrelevant to the plot. Come on, <b>Mead</b>. Your readers are not stupid. Everyone knows you just want a way of describing what Mae is wearing. Having it done by the guy who obviously wants her in his bed would be a bonus, right?<br><br>Not convinced?<br><br><blockquote>He always took inventory of her clothes, and she was casual today in a damask patterned blouse and jeans that did incredible things for her legs.</blockquote><br><blockquote>Mae was at the height of style, as always, even when casual. Her mother's dress was from last year. A small detail, but notable among castals.</blockquote><br><br>No straight man cares that much about clothing. In the words of an ex boyfriend: <b>"Who cares what you wear? I'm imagining you without it, anyway."</b><br><br>But enough speculation on character sexual-orientation. <br><br>Another problem I had with <i>Gameboard</i> was how needlessly <i>long</i> it was. <b>Most of the scenes and even <i>characters</i> were completely useless</b>, weren't it for their future roles in (I suspect) the sequels.<br>Tessa was completely useless. I certainly did not need to go into her highschool life. I was under the impression, after all, that I was reading an <i>adult</i> novel. However, it seems <b>Mead</b> simply cannot help herself, and a novel is incomplete without petty highschool scenes.<br>Her role in "solving the mystery" is also a complete boner-killer. <b>How the plot panned out was a complete let-down.</b> After all that build-up, after all that talk about how intelligent and observant and yaddah-yaddah-yaddah Justin was, we had everything solved by some <i>random boy approaching Tessa and virtually handing out the answers to her</i>??? I call bullshit and sheer laziness.<br><br>Admittedly, the world-building must have required a lot of thought and planning. <b>Mead did a sufficient job of fleshing out her world, coming up with a relatively fresh take on a futuristic society</b>. The downside is that I just couldn't give a single care about any of it.<br>I couldn't sympathize with the .... Provincials? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(See, I can't even remember the terms used, and I've only finished this novel literally ten minutes ago) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> despite how unevenly handed their lives were. The blatant classism was there, and I <i>knew</i> it was supposed to be strong in this world <b>Mead</b> created, but it simply fell flat and <i>"whatever"</i> to me.<br>That's what happens when you try to disguise a YA novel as an <i>adult</i> book, but still have all the childish and trivial tropes make a blatantly strong appearance. I just can't take anything seriously.<br><br>And when I say "childish and trivial", I am mostly talking about our characters. As much as <b>Mead</b> tried to provide a deep background for them, there are still a few things that comes to the foreground, to which I just can't help associate to her previous series, <i>Vampire Academy</i>:<br><br>-Forbidden Love.<br><br>-Perfectly perfect characters: gorgeous heroine who is Da Bomb, who EVERYONE wants. Gorgeous hero who wants her but can't have her.<br><br>-Sexually aware and open heroine.<br><br>-Sexual tension I could not find remotely panty-wetting.<br><br>And of course:<br>-A "body-guard" heroine, who has to use her awesome strength and awesome perfectness to protect someone she's been assigned to.<br><br>Maybe <b>Mead</b> has some kind of fetish to this trope, since it seems she can't stop writing about it? Or can she simply not think of anything better?<br><br>The reason this frustrates me so much is because I <i>hated</i> Vampire Academy, and I was absolutely completely and utterly looking forward to something <b>completely different</b> in this "Adult" novel of hers.<br>Well, the plot may be different. The world may be different. But underneath all that, the blueprint is still the same.<br><br><br>***<br><i>you can also find my reviews at my blog</i><br>***<br><br>
  <a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="elfswood" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404185i/786473.jpg" width="220 px" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
<br><br><br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>9 Jan '12</u>
</b><br><b>Richelle Mead</b> and I didn't hit it off too well with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172807749" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Vampire Academy</i>
</a>; but I was turned off by the actual <i>story</i> rather than <b>Mead</b>'s writing style, so I'm very much willing to give her another chance.<br><br>Not to mention this has nothing to do with <i>Vampire Academy</i>; fingers crossed for something different and refreshing!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_440326127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440326127" />
    <a title="Siiri (Little Pieces of Imagination)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination"><img alt="Siiri (Little Pieces of Imagination)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326300005p2/7399193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440326127?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siiri (Little Pieces of Imagination)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siiri (Little Pieces of Imagination)" href="/user/show/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination">Siiri (Little Pieces of Imagination)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=first-of-the-series">first-of-the-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=arc_rc">arc_rc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399193-siiri-little-pieces-of-imagination?shelf=shipping-these-dorks">shipping-these-dorks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440326127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer149863437773530306"><b>An ARC was provided in exchange for an honest review</b><br/><br/>I have read 3 series by Richelle Mead and have yet to read a book by her that would be a disappointment. Seriously! I know I have given two stars to Frostbite (Vampire Academy #2) for instance, but it was just a rating based on how I felt it being a little weaker than the rest of the books in that series. If I didn’t delve on those things, I’d give them all 5 stars since her books seriously never disappoint. Gameboard of the Gods is the first b</span>
  <span id="freeText149863437773530306" style="display:none"><b>An ARC was provided in exchange for an honest review</b><br><br>I have read 3 series by Richelle Mead and have yet to read a book by her that would be a disappointment. Seriously! I know I have given two stars to Frostbite (Vampire Academy #2) for instance, but it was just a rating based on how I felt it being a little weaker than the rest of the books in that series. If I didn’t delve on those things, I’d give them all 5 stars since her books seriously never disappoint. Gameboard of the Gods is the first book in one of my newest favorite series.<br><br><i>"We're pieces on a gameboard, Dr. March, and some of us are more powerful than the others. You. Me. Her. We're the ones that gods want. We're the ones they're fighting over." – page 443 of the ARC.</i><br><br><b>The story.</b> In a futuristic world, Mae Koskinen is a praetorian – a fierce Nordic soldier who is a part of the RUNA’s military. What makes her so special is that she is a gorgeous, flawless castal. Castals aka pure bloods have suffered from different illnesses, but Mae’s beauty is untouched. Justin March is a servitor in exile. He is called back by his former bosses to investigate mysterious, unsolvable religious murders. He is a plebian aka a normal, mixed-blooded person. Along with them we have another MC – Tessa Cruz – a teenage girl who is an outsider from a province.<br><br><b>My thoughts.</b> First of all, it was a beast! 464 pages full of action. I’m usually not that keen on third person POVs, but Ms. Mead really made it work. Through Tessa’s eyes we see the true colors of RUNA and thanks to her, we learn the most about RUNA as she’s in the same position as we are – a newcomer. We get this futuristic society in its complex world of religion and atheism, advanced technology and fake smiles. At first it all felt very complicated to me, especially since I’m not a native English speaker, but as the novel progressed, the more at home I felt in this world. I liked how the technology advancements were new and intriguing, but not completely incomprehensible to grasp for our minds. Also, the further I read, the more the mythology part came into the picture.<br><br>We have an excellent cast of characters and they are all so very different, flawed and difficult to crack. (I didn't care for Tessa as much as I cared for Mae and Justing though.) I was a big fan of how Richelle managed to keep me invested in the mystery and keep the wheels spinning in my head, yet I didn’t figure it all out beforehand, especially who the god bidding on Justin was. That, I should have figured out sooner! I also loved how the romance between Justin and Mae was there, but they’re so proud and stubborn to admit their feelings (even to themselves) that we’ll have to have them fight their feelings for quite some time in this series. Maybe Justin and Mae's POVs, regarding the tone and the thoughts, melted together for me a little, but I still enjoyed them thoroughly. <br><br>To sum up my thoughts, I’d say that if you’re looking for a read full of mythology, suspense, mystery, character-built and well-written plot with a touch of romance, pick this up! Richelle Mead has a way of writing books that suck you in like no other and don’t let go until you’ve devoured all of it with your nails bitten. I am eagerly anticipating what’s next to come in this crazy world where humans are the pawns of gods in this intriguing dystopian gameboard. This book is surely not to be missed!<br><br><i>Original thoughts before reading: Holy smoke! O_O I got my first ever Dutton arc. Whoop, whoop! Oh, did I mention it's freaking Richelle Mead? <s>I feel nothing.</s> I feel everything. (Sorry, I just finished Shatter Me by Tahereh Mafi.) ANYHOW, my friend SpongeBob SquarePants knows exactly how I feel;-)</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395268ra/761239.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="149863437773530306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_512017575" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/512017575" />
    <a title="♥ Becky  22 " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7778906-becky-22"><img alt="♥ Becky  22 " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442311403p2/7778906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512017575?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ Becky  22 " class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ Becky  22 " href="/user/show/7778906-becky-22">♥ Becky  22 </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17999706-gameboard-of-the-gods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7778906-becky-22?shelf=comes-out-in-2013">comes-out-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7778906-becky-22?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7778906-becky-22?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512017575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13323654317420412330">★★★☆☆/☆☆☆☆☆ <b> 3.5 stars, but only because the last 20 pages were kickass.<br/>I LOVE the concept, but this book was way, way too drawn out. </b><br/>This review is spoiler-free!<br/>_____________________________________<br/>_____________________________________<br/><br/><b>What it’s about, in one sentence</b><br/>Justin has been exciled from his home country (the RUNA) for mysterious reasons, but is brought back at the beginning of the story, because they need him to investigate a murder case that may, or may not involve supernatural element</span>
  <span id="freeText13323654317420412330" style="display:none">★★★☆☆/☆☆☆☆☆ <b> 3.5 stars, but only because the last 20 pages were kickass.<br />I LOVE the concept, but this book was way, way too drawn out. </b><br />This review is spoiler-free!<br />_____________________________________<br />_____________________________________<br /><br /><b>What it’s about, in one sentence</b><br />Justin has been exciled from his home country (the RUNA) for mysterious reasons, but is brought back at the beginning of the story, because they need him to investigate a murder case that may, or may not involve supernatural elements. (It's a bit more complicated than that, but there you go.)<br /><br /><b>My thoughts</b><br />Gameboard of the Gods is complicated, and too drawn out for my taste, but it is also original and super interesting. This book has about 500 pages and with the amount of things that happen in it, it could be 100 pages shorter. I struggled through the middle, but I never wanted to not finish the book, because the mystery the story is set around, is really, really captivating. <br />So when things did happen, they were very intense, and I felt myself getting sucked into the story again. <br /><br />The world this story is set in is SO well thought out. I’ve read a lot of dystopian novels, but I don’t think I’ve ever come across a world this detailed and thought through. <br /><br />The story is told from the switching 3rd person POVs of Justin, Mae (his praetorian bodyguard. Praetorians are scary as shit. They have this implant that gives them superhuman strength and they don’t need to sleep. They freak me about a bit.), and Tessa (a 16-year-old girl from one of the Provinces. She’s the only one who can see the RUNA for what it is, because she didn’t grow up there). <br /><br />Justin was easily my favorite character, and, as a matter of fact, he was the only character I really liked. Tessa was meh, and for some reason I couldn’t stand Mae for the better part of the book. (But those are just personal opinions. You might love them all!)<br /><br />This is not a quick, fun read. This is a pay-close-attention-while-you’re-reading-otherwise-you’ll-be-totally-lost-in-the-world-of-the-RUNA kind of book. <br />Despite its flaws I enjoyed this book and I will probably be reading the next one in the series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13323654317420412330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_326239231" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326239231" />
    <a title="shre ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5800904-shre"><img alt="shre ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585531738p2/5800904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326239231?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shre ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shre ♡" href="/user/show/5800904-shre">shre ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326239231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2650223705488137086">.......I don't know...why...but I feel like like Mead should just stick to vampires >.> Not that I didn't like this but it just doesn't come across as something I'd like to read again..or yah. Either way, it was good just not great :) Review to come. </span>

<div id="review_474808054" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474808054" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474808054?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474808054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2037550099528672654">For a futuristic society, Gameboard of the Gods is definitely not progressive.<br/><br/>In a world of religious extremists, RUNA (Republic of United North America) have established themselves as the superior state where their attitude, technology and lifestyle is clearly ‘better’ than others. Here, you’d encounter extreme castal segregation between the plebians (residents of RUNA) and patricians who are blonde hair and blue eyed and clearly different. All plebians look the same and have been conceived in </span>
  <span id="freeText2037550099528672654" style="display:none">For a futuristic society, Gameboard of the Gods is definitely not progressive.<br /><br />In a world of religious extremists, RUNA (Republic of United North America) have established themselves as the superior state where their attitude, technology and lifestyle is clearly ‘better’ than others. Here, you’d encounter extreme castal segregation between the plebians (residents of RUNA) and patricians who are blonde hair and blue eyed and clearly different. All plebians look the same and have been conceived in a petrie dish whereas patricians are more superior because they’ve clung onto their cultural heritage. The plebians despise the patricians who live on old money and the patricians look down at disdain at the plebians who are the ‘lowly’ class. And then there are genmans who live in the rural areas, who are looked down upon by the plebians. It’s just a book full of cultural and race segregation and snobbery.<br /><br />If you haven’t noticed already, there’s a lot of confusing, brand new concepts introduced here. This is only a small sample of what’s to come. Gameboard of the Gods is not an easy book to digest and read, and if you’re a fan of Richelle Mead’s previous paranormal books, this is on a league of its own in complex world building and new concepts.<br /><br />If I didn’t read the blurb and hadn’t known the society was meant to be set in the future, I would have forgiven a lot of things. Despite the advanced technology, these people live like they’re back in Ancient Rome with the segregation and the punishing people for the worship of the Gods and slight hint of magic existing.<br /><br />Continued on the <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/05/31/gameboard-of-the-gods-by-richelle-mead-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence Book Blog. </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2037550099528672654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_29547345'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29547345-struck"><img alt="Struck (Phoebe Meadows, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1458312530l/29547345._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oOQ6hf5PQfdTyQ0t14ZLgKzanMIRhGzjEBIG6KazU/XEESc1jDZGa0N6jBJ8FVbvPxYC8JVoJ8suZdclBzpQWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+nKbmWg7uon1EiP2TC+stY5AZ/YTz4k/86ts81ZYDA6eh4YpGkK9FeWhosnnvLHaHYz5xJcjwhfN3L0+99EPow==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10487233447111124847">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br/><br/>A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away f</span>
  <span id="freeText10487233447111124847" style="display:none">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br /><br />A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away from books (either reading or writing them), she enjoys bad reality TV, traveling, trying interesting cocktails, and shopping for dresses. She's a self-professed coffee addict and has a passion for all things wacky and humorous.<br /></span>

      $('bookCover_22057201').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
